Britain States Its Position on the War Debt Issue 83

Based on the Principle of Not Exceeding the Lausanne Agreement

▲ Reuters, London, 2nd It is believed here that Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain's speech at a reception for American journalists on the 1st has created the impression that the British government hopes that negotiations between Britain and the United States will be limited to war debts. Responsible parties in London issued statements clarifying that the solution to the war debt issue is based on the principle of not exceeding the agreements of the Lausanne Conference and not infringing on the rights of other countries. As for issues related to war debts, there are no restrictions on discussion.

▲ Havas Agency, London, 2nd Chancellor Chamberlain's declaration to the American press completely rejects various conditions proposed by the United States for a satisfactory solution to the war debt issue. It is generally believed that the Chancellor's rebuttal of the American conditions one by one is intended to maintain the principles that Britain has always adhered to, that is, the cancellation of war debts is the best solution, and its impact is the same as the cancellation of reparations to Germany. The cancellation of war debts will relieve the world economy of its burden, and the good results it will produce will be more than enough to compensate the United States. From this, it can be seen that Britain is still adhering to the policies it has followed for the past ten years and the principle that European debtor countries should unite, as declared in Britain's previous notes before December 15 of last year. Britain has always advocated that the war debt issue be resolved in the manner of the Lausanne Conference, that is, to cancel it fundamentally and unconditionally. This time, the Chancellor's declaration rebutting the American conditions, even disapproving of the method of deferral, makes the idea of Britain's unconditional cancellation of war debts even more credible.

▲ Guomin News Agency, Washington, 2nd Today, US Senator Robinson proposed in the Senate that Berridge's negotiation of war debts abroad violates federal law, and demanded that the Senate order the State Department to recall him. Therefore, Roosevelt's friends immediately telegraphed Ross, and received a reply stating that he had not authorized Berridge to engage in any negotiations. Robinson's move was directed at Roosevelt, because the radicals of the Republican Party mostly oppose Ross's presiding over informal negotiations at this time.

Roosevelt Announces Unemployment Relief Plan 84

▲ Guomin News Agency, Warm Springs, 2nd President-elect Roosevelt is now planning to develop the Muscle Shoals in the Tennessee River, establish a large hydroelectric plant, and absorb nitrogen from the air to manufacture nitrates. This plan was originally initiated by President Wilson, who wanted to manufacture nitrates for the Allied forces to use in combat. When the Democratic government left office in 1921, the Republican Party passed a bill to stop state-owned operations and lease the completed hydroelectric plant to private individuals. Now Ross is seeking to continue Wilson's legacy and expand it. It is estimated that 71,000 people can be employed in the first year, and up to 200,000 people can be employed thereafter, which is also a strategy to solve the unemployment problem.

▲ Reuters, Warm Springs, 2nd President-elect Roosevelt announced to a reporter today his domestic tax plan, which, if implemented, could provide work for tens of thousands of unemployed people in the United States. This plan includes afforestation, water conservancy, and agricultural improvement. It is expected that the distribution of population between urban and rural areas can be equalized as a result. Roosevelt predicted that the experiment of this plan could accommodate 200,000 unemployed people in the Tennessee Valley alone. Roosevelt hopes to implement this plan elsewhere in the country, from the Allegheny Mountains to the Pacific Coast, so that he can relieve unemployment and eliminate the ills of industrial concentration.

Investigation of Soviet Military Preparations (Moscow Correspondence) 85

Although the Soviet Union is today a nation that steadfastly adheres to a policy of peace, its military preparations emphasize defense over offense. Furthermore, due to its ongoing efforts in social construction, its military arrangements are not as advanced as those of other countries. However, because of the differences in its ideology and policies, the capitalist nations of the world are watching it intently, ready to pounce at any weakness. The recent ominous situation in the Far East has been a major threat to the Soviet Union. Therefore, while social construction is being vigorously accelerated, preparations in the military sphere are also increasing daily. During the first Five-Year Plan, the military aspect was specifically shortened to be completed in three years (the army and navy budget was 760 million rubles in 1927 and increased to 1.28 billion rubles in 1932). This shows the extent to which it is intensifying its defenses. In the world struggles of the near future, the Soviet Union will undoubtedly occupy an extremely important position, especially on the Far Eastern stage, where it will be a key player. Therefore, the current state of its military preparations should be something that the people of our nation are eager to know. A brief report is presented below.

(Outline of the Military System) The Soviet military system is based on conscription, stipulating a service period from age nineteen to forty, totaling twenty-two years. Before conscription, there are two years of preparatory education, followed by five years of active service and fifteen years in the reserves. According to the Soviet Constitution, non-laborers are not allowed to serve in the military, as military service is considered an honor and a right. Therefore, Soviet youths, upon reaching adulthood, all serve in the military. The Soviet army can be divided into two types: the regular army and the reserve army. The reserve army is required to undergo eight to eleven months of military education over five years. This system is intended to disseminate military education to the general male population in the most economical way, and it is enforced by the government. This shows that military education in the Soviet Union is exceptionally widespread. In the event of war, the number of soldiers able to participate in combat would be enormous.

(Overview of Military Strength) The Soviet Union's peacetime military strength is approximately 1.3 million people, including over seventy infantry divisions, a dozen cavalry divisions, about ten independent brigades, and other units such as aviation and chemical warfare units. Among these land forces, eight divisions are stationed in the Leningrad Military District, twelve divisions in the Moscow Military District, twenty-one divisions in the Ukrainian Military District, six divisions in the Volga Military District, eight divisions in the North Caucasus Military District, twelve divisions in the Belorussian Military District, three divisions in the Siberian Military District, seven divisions in the Far East, four divisions and two brigades in Central Asia, and seven divisions and one brigade in the Independent Caucasus area. Their combat capabilities are described in the following sections: ① Infantry: Each division is divided into three regiments, each regiment containing one signals platoon, one reconnaissance platoon, three assault battalions, nine companies (nine light machine gun platoons), three heavy machine gun companies, three battalion artillery platoons, one regimental artillery battalion (two companies), two chemical platoons, three assault platoons, and two machine gun platoons. Each division is equipped with a total of 162 light machine guns, 108 heavy machine guns, and 36 field guns, as well as hand grenades. ② Cavalry: Soviet cavalry has always been considered among the best in the world. In the 1920 Russo-Polish War, Russia prevailed due to its superior cavalry. However, in modern tactics, cavalry is generally considered less useful. Therefore, while the Soviet Union has excellent cavalry, whether it will occupy a significant position on the battlefield in the future remains a question. Nevertheless, in warfare on vast plains, cavalry is still extremely necessary for communication and transportation. ③ Armored Vehicle Units: Armored vehicles were first used by the British army on the Somme battlefield in September 1916. After the British army launched a major offensive with hundreds of armored vehicles against the German army on the Cambrai battlefield in 1917, all countries spared no expense in manufacturing them. The Soviet Union has also been rapidly improving and increasing its armored vehicle units in recent years. ④ Aviation: The Soviet air force was quite weak ten years ago. In 1922, it had only twenty squadrons, which increased to seventy-eight squadrons in 1925 and one hundred and four squadrons in 1928. Currently, it has reached over two hundred squadrons, including 194 land aircraft squadrons and 20 seaplane squadrons, totaling 2,200 aircraft. The Soviet Union plans to add another two hundred squadrons within ten years. Regarding the aviation manufacturing industry, there are now twenty-five factories nationwide, producing heavy bombers with a total weight of twenty tons, which are comparable to those produced by Germany and Italy. At the same time, the entire Soviet population is particularly enthusiastic about the development of aviation. There is a National Defense Aviation and Chemical Association, which is a semi-official organization with over 17 million members. The mission of this association is to conduct military training for the people under the guidance of the government. It has established military chemical research institutes, clubs, shooting clubs, and equestrian clubs in various locations, with particular emphasis on the study of aviation and poison gas. In addition, it has established numerous aviation schools to train general aviation technicians. Because the Soviet Union has vast lands, few railways, and inconvenient transportation, it is urgently seeking the development of aviation. In peacetime, it can be used for transportation, and in wartime, it can facilitate military operations. Last year, the Soviet Union invested a total of 150 million rubles in aviation construction. The aviation lines reached 49,000 kilometers last year. All of this is the result of the efforts of the Soviet people and their government. ⑤ Military Chemistry: Modern warfare will evolve into chemical warfare. All countries are striving to refine their research in military chemistry. The Soviet Union also has unusually strict military facilities in this regard. It strives to popularize national military chemical education and currently has three chemical warfare schools, six chemical weapons research institutes, and four chemical weapons manufacturing plants.

(Soldier Capabilities) Soviet soldiers have the special characteristic of being particularly hardy. Therefore, if they can be given good equipment, complete military education, and led by outstanding commanders, they can become the strongest army in the world. This is recognized by people around the world. In the old imperial era, due to the lack of universal education, the majority of soldiers were illiterate. They frequently missed many opportunities in battle due to a lack of knowledge. Since the revolution, due to the government's efforts to promote universal education, illiteracy has decreased daily. Soldiers have received considerable education before enlisting and continue to receive training after enlisting. The results of soldier training are excellent. Special attention is paid to spiritual education, that is, political education. The purpose is to make every person a communist cell. Therefore, Soviet soldiers can be considered excellent soldiers in modern times. Unfortunately, the strategic abilities of middle and lower-ranking military officers are mostly very immature. This is the biggest shortcoming of the Soviet army.

(Treatment of Soldiers) The Soviet government's treatment of soldiers is very comprehensive. It pays special attention not only to active duty soldiers but also to veterans, providing benefits such as retirement and death benefits, subsidies for childbirth, assistance with family medical expenses, free transportation, preferential treatment for children's education, and so on. There are also noteworthy aspects of the treatment of active duty soldiers, such as ① preserving the farms assigned to enlisted active duty soldiers on their behalf, ② allowing them to receive labor funds or unemployment benefits during refresher training, ③ reserving positions to be filled by veterans in order to avoid unemployment after their service is completed, ④ providing considerable tax exemptions for postal taxes and transportation costs, and ⑤ offering extremely favorable housing allocation. These types of benefits for soldiers would be unusually difficult to implement in other countries, but they are extremely easy to implement in the Soviet Union because its social system is inherently like this. Even for people who are not soldiers, life is already very comfortable.

(Relationship with the Far East) Here, we must add that since the Eastern Province Incident, the Soviet Union has increased its troops in the Far East. According to Japanese sources, the Soviet military strength in the Far East has reached more than 100,000. However, as Japanese forces have shown a tendency to advance rapidly northwestward from the mainland, the Soviet Union cannot but take appropriate precautions for its own security. The Soviet authorities have repeatedly stated that the Soviet Union has no intention of challenging any country, but if other countries intend to invade the Soviet Union, then the Soviet Union will defend itself. Therefore, we cannot say that the Soviet Union's troop increase in the Far East means that it is preparing for a conflict with Japan, nor can we say that the Soviet Union has reached a considerable compromise with Japan simply because it has not made any active statement. We believe that the Soviet Union has its own definite position, which cannot be expressed until the appropriate time. (January 5)

Planned Actions of the Japanese Army in Hankou 86

Strict Security in the Japanese Concession, All Residents Armed

Officials and Merchants Hold Important Meetings Repeatedly, Situation Becomes Increasingly Tense

Hankou Correspondence: Since the start of the fighting in Jehol, the Japanese army and navy stationed in Hankou have been actively preparing for military action. In recent days, they have been installing artillery positions, moving warships, and forcing all residents to arm themselves. The tension is palpable, and a conflict seems imminent. It has been observed that whenever there is a conflict between China and Japan, the Japanese always prepare for war in Hankou to disrupt our rear. What they are doing now is indeed a planned action, not merely a demonstration of force. I will now report on the recent situation in detail.

(Land and Sea Security in the Japanese Concession) The Japanese concession in Hankou is located in the far east of the city, bordering the Special District No. 1. It reaches the Yangtze River in the south and the Pinghan Railway in the north. It is a place that harbors dirt and filth. It is as if there is a separate world within Hankou City. Recently, due to military arrangements, the scene is extremely grim. Artillery positions have been set up on the roads bordering the Chinese and Japanese areas, with the largest being up to 20 centimeters in caliber. Preparations are also being made to erect electric fences. Police are now on double duty, and telephones have been installed at all guard posts. Key locations, such as the consulate, the naval landing force headquarters, the administrative committee of the residents' association, the police station, and the police department, all have air defense facilities. Traffic along the naval docks on the Japanese border is cut off at 9 p.m. The river surface is originally stationed with the Ataka, Uji, Tsushima, Hira, and Kotaka warships. They are all connected. It is impossible to ascertain how many naval personnel are stationed there. It can only be seen that they are conducting landing exercises every day and maneuvering artillery after returning to the ships. The Kotaka warship was ordered to go to Changsha one day, and the Ataka and other four warships remained in Hankou. Commander Sakano of the 1st Overseas Dispatch Fleet is stationed here in charge.

(Residents Armed, Okamura's Bold Words) Naval Commander Sakano summoned naval officers and soldiers from various warships at the non-commissioned officer assembly hall one day and gave a speech. The content is unknown. At the same time, Army Attaché Okamura declared to the Japanese residents that the country's Third Overseas Dispatch Fleet had a strong presence in the Yangtze River. The ammunition currently on each warship is sufficient for eight hours of continuous firing every day, enough for ten days. He also ordered all residents to arm themselves and receive military training. The first batch has been trained and matured, and the second and third batches are being trained intensively. All of them will be issued firearms for use. There are currently over 1,900 Japanese residents, excluding prostitutes and children. Among them, there are no fewer than 1,000 strong men. If they are organized, it would be equivalent to a regiment of conscripts. There are also 147 veterans and 40 members of the youth league who can be conscripted as soldiers in case of emergency. In peacetime, they use retirement or being in the countryside to cover up the eyes and ears of foreigners. It is equivalent to having two companies of reservists.

(Officials and Merchants Meeting to Plot Against Us) Important personnel from the Japanese army and navy held a meeting a few days ago to discuss the military arrangements for the Yangtze River. It has now concluded. The consulate held another secret meeting yesterday, attended by many important merchants. Military personnel also participated. The important resolutions are not easy to ascertain. What is known is that ① they secretly contacted rice merchants in the Chinese area to purchase large quantities of rice for hoarding in preparation for emergencies; ② the traffic office in the Japanese area is heavily guarded and will erect electric fences if necessary; ③ they are buying over Chinese traitors to inspect our fortifications and the locations where our troops are stationed or transferred; ④ all Japanese residents in Hankou will be issued firearms; and ⑤ the consul will convene a secret meeting once a week. In addition, Kiyokawa, the head of the administrative committee of the Japanese residents' association, convened a business conference of Japanese merchants, attended by more than 40 people. It was decided that all merchants doing business in the Chinese area must report the type, value, quantity, and business conditions of their goods in detail every day for reference.

(Extensive Establishment of Agencies to Probe Our Military Situation) The Japanese are extremely attentive to our military situation. In recent days, they have dispatched ruffians, disguised as Chinese or using Chinese traitors, to Wuchang, Hanyang, Guishan, the arsenal, and the towns downstream of Tianjia Town to conduct reconnaissance. Their movements are secretive. Recently, they have established two intelligence agencies: one is the Naval Landing Force Intelligence Department, commanded by naval officer Tajiri, and the other is the Japanese Police Department's Higher Section and the United Electric News Agency, commanded by the Japanese Consulate. They subscribe to as many as twenty-two major and minor newspapers in Wuhan and Shanghai and compile all anti-Japanese articles. They have detailed investigations into the names, brief histories, and sources of income of the responsible persons and editors of each newspaper, as well as the number of copies sold. They have also drawn up charts of the locations of military installations and the Special District No. 1 and the territories under the jurisdiction of the 13 districts that are adjacent to the Japanese concession. Yesterday, Japanese naval and army officers inspected the Japanese concession for a week and looked at the watchtowers near Liujiamiao. Their probing of our military situation can be described as meticulous.

(Hiding Traitors, Colluding with Bad Elements) The Japanese concession has always been tolerant of our country's rebels, not only political prisoners. Recently, it was discovered that Zheng Jianghao, the secretary of the Transportation Department of the puppet Manchurian state, was hiding in the Japanese concession. Zheng is originally from Hubei. After the establishment of the puppet organization, he took on this position and came to Hankou under the orders of the puppet regime. He has been protected by the Japanese and lives at No. 19 Dawamai Street, the residence of Liu Qiangsheng, in the Japanese concession. He is now eager to flee back to the Northeast and has decided to wait for Commander Sakano of Japan to go to Shanghai and accompany him. In addition, there are ruffians colluding with Chinese bad elements such as Lin Runbo to smuggle firearms and ammunition to bandits and local bandits. The ruffians are responsible for transporting them. They also forge various banknotes of 10 yuan, 5 yuan, and 1 yuan from the Henan Farmers and Workers Bank and the Hankou Central and Southern Bank, as well as subsidiary coins of 5 jiao, 2 jiao, and 1 jiao from the provincial bank, which are carried by Lin and others to various places for use. One purpose is to disrupt our country's finances, and the other is to purchase large quantities of grain. (February 2)

The Southwest Has Decided on a Major Plan to Resist Japan 87

Bai Chongxi Also Attends the Meeting in Guangzhou

Cai Tingkai Advocates Unity and Solidarity Against External Aggression

Huang Shaohong Takes the Results Back to Nanjing to Report

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since Li Zongren, Huang Shaohong, and Cai Tingkai successively arrived in Guangzhou, Bai Chongxi from Nanning also came to Guangzhou from Nanning on January 23, accompanied by Ye Qi, the Chief of Staff of the Fourth Army Group. On the 25th, he arrived in Wuzhou and transferred to a steamer eastward in the afternoon. On the 26th, he arrived at Sanshui Hekou at 1:00 p.m. Upon receiving the news, the political circles here immediately sent a Guangzhou-Sanshui floral car to welcome him. Military and political figures and personnel from the rear office of the Fourth Army Group also went to Shiwetang Station to welcome him. Bai's special train arrived at 4:20 p.m. Bai then took a car to Li Zongren's residence in Mapenggang, East Mountain, to visit Li. After talking for a while, he went to visit Huang Shaohong and Chen Jitang. After finishing, he returned to Li's residence in Mapenggang to stay. The Southwest Political Affairs Committee hosted a banquet at 12:00 noon on the 27th, inviting Chen Jitang, Li Zongren, Deng Zeru, Zou Lu, Lin Yunhai, Liu Luyin, Xiang Hanping, Miao Peinan, Ye Qi, Wang Zanbin, Liu Jiwen, and dozens of others because Cai Tingkai, Huang Shaohong, and Bai Chongxi had successively arrived. The atmosphere was very pleasant during the banquet, and it lasted until 1:00 p.m. In the evening of the 27th, Chen Jitang hosted another banquet for Cai, Huang, Bai, and others at his private residence in the Model Village. It is said that Bai's important purpose in coming here is to consolidate the Southwest's defenses and discuss important issues related to resisting Japan.

As for Cai Tingkai's consultations in Guangdong on the major plan to resist Japan, it has recently been heard that results have been achieved. According to Cai, it is inconvenient to disclose details about national defense and military affairs to the outside world. However, resisting Japan and suppressing the Communists must have a comprehensive plan and unified solidarity. No single aspect can be carried out independently. Secondly, consolidating national defense should be planned at all times and not only when disaster strikes. Our country has always been negligent about national defense. Therefore, we suffered a lot in the Songhu Anti-Japanese War last year. It is urgent for the provinces in the Southwest to prepare for national defense. For example, Guangdong has a very long coastline, and we can be attacked anytime and anywhere. Therefore, the military arrangements for coastal defense fortresses are particularly urgent. Recent war trophies, such as fighter planes and new-style guns and artillery, should be urgently stored. However, some people in the country do not know how to plan national defense and use the few national defense weapons they have for internal conflicts. This is truly heartbreaking. I hope that the people of the country will prioritize the country in the future and make consolidating the country's territory the prerequisite, and stop starting civil wars due to private views. My telegrams a few days ago called for the cessation of internal conflicts, which were triggered by the Sichuan-Guizhou civil war. I urge all rulers to abandon private struggles and prepare to sacrifice for the preservation of national territory. As for the issue of suppressing the Communists, it is as important as resisting Japan. Being destroyed by the Communists is the same as being destroyed by Japan. Our army has been making steady progress in suppressing the Communists in Fujian. There are now no large Communist bandits hiding in the entire Fujian area. There are occasional sporadic local Communists appearing, but they are not a cause for concern. Changting was originally accessible and could have been entered by a direct drive, but it was not possible due to insufficient preparations for supplies. The Communist Party was originally one of the political parties. Foreign Communist parties engage in political struggles in peacetime, but once there is a foreign invasion, political struggles immediately cease, and they unite to resist foreign aggression. If our country's Communist Party can realize this in the future, prioritize the country, and act as a vanguard against external aggression, then the central government may give them a chance to reform.

As for Huang Shaohong's biggest task in coming south, it is to unite the Southwest to be consistent with the central government in resisting external aggression. Because the central government already has a comprehensive plan to resist external aggression, it must obtain the understanding of the leaders of the Southwest and stop publishing divergent opinions. Then the plan will be easier to implement. Cai Tingkai's coming to Guangdong also shares the same view as Huang. It is said that after repeated meetings, the Southwest has unanimously accepted the central government's comprehensive plan to resist external aggression. At the same time, the three provinces of Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian must also be prepared. It is slightly heard that on the active side, each of the three provinces plans to select a certain number of strong men to form volunteer armies, ready to be mobilized at any time. As for handling this matter, a Guangdong-Guangxi-Fujian Provincial Volunteer Army Military Commission will be established to be responsible. The members of the commission will be senior military officers appointed by the three provinces. The volunteer armies of the three provinces are currently preparing to be trained. Once Huang Shaohong returns to Nanjing to report and waits for the central government's order, they can be mobilized. On the passive side, that is, to carry out coastal fortress arrangements for national defense in the southwestern provinces, and to pay close attention to transportation. The leaders and generals of the three provinces also held a meeting to discuss this in detail. Decisions were made on issues such as how many troops should be stationed in the fortresses in the southwestern provinces in the future, how many more artillery positions should be added, and whether senior officials should be assigned to the fortresses. The above active and passive plans have all been drafted in special projects, and they are all handed over to Huang Shaohong to take back to Nanjing to be reviewed by the central government. After the central government approves and replies, they will be implemented accordingly. Huang completed his mission and left Guangdong on the morning of the 30th. Bai Chongxi went to Hong Kong with him. After meeting with a certain tycoon in Hong Kong, Huang took a steamer to Shanghai and returned to Nanjing, and Bai also took a steamer from Hong Kong back to Guangxi. Cai Tingkai still needs to stay for a few more days and will return to Fujian after meeting with Yu Hanmou, the commander of the First Army. (January 30 evening)

He Chengjun and Shao Lizhi Arrive in Wuhan Together 88

Immediately Proceeding from Wuhan to Jiangxi to Meet Chairman Chiang Kai-shek

A dispatch from Hankou reports that He Chengjun, the Pacification Commissioner for Hubei, and Shao Lizhi, Chairman of the Gansu Provincial Government, needing to report on military and political affairs to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, agreed to travel from Xi'an to Nanjing together. Learning that Chairman Chiang had departed for Nanchang, they changed their route, taking the Longhai Railway to the Pinghan Railway, going south to Wuhan and then on to Nanchang. Mr. Shao, together with Cai Jingchen, Secretary-General of the Gansu Provincial Government, arrived in Xi'an by Eurasian Aviation plane from Lanzhou at 5:00 PM on January 28th. He met with He Chengjun and Yang Hucheng. At 9:00 AM on January 31st, He and Shao departed in four cars for Tongguan, where they transferred to a special train on the Longhai Railway, heading east. They arrived in Zhengzhou at 8:00 AM on the 1st of this month. At 8:00 PM that afternoon, they switched to a special train on the Pinghan Railway heading south. They arrived in Wuhan around 5:00 PM on the 2nd. They are scheduled to take a steamer to Xun on the evening of the 3rd, transferring to Nanchang to meet Chairman Chiang. According to the statements issued by He and Shao, they are as follows:

(He Chengjun's Statement) He stated briefly, "I received orders from Commander-in-Chief Chiang to depart from Wuhan for Xi'an on December 26th of last year to establish an administrative office to command various units to pursue and suppress the bandit troops of Xu Xiangqian. After arriving in Xi'an, I immediately discussed and determined a pursuit and suppression plan with Director Yang Hucheng, instructing the various units responsible for bandit suppression to diligently pursue and suppress the bandits in various directions according to the established steps. I also telegraphed Sichuanese military generals, Liu Cunhou, the Border Defense Commissioner of Sichuan and Shaanxi, and Tian Songyao, the commander of the 29th Army, to send troops to block them. Xu's bandits suffered heavy losses in Shaanxi, realizing that the National Army was powerful and could not be resisted. They resorted to their old tricks, avoiding strength and attacking weakness. After passing through southern Shaanxi, they did not engage the National Army, but devoted themselves to fleeing, and finally fled to the mountains near Tongjiang in northern Sichuan. Shaanxi troops have now reached suitable locations and made proper deployments. The Sichuanese troops of Tian Songyao have also been fully mobilized, totaling four divisions and three brigades. Director Yang Hucheng and Army Commander Tian Songyao are respectively responsible for command. Tian himself is personally supervising the suppression in Nanyuan and has already departed. The Gansu side has also dispatched considerable forces to garrison key passes to prevent their escape. The remaining strength of the remnant bandits is no more than 6,000 firearms. They lack ammunition and supplies. With our large army suppressing them, they will be unable to withstand a single blow. However, recently the weather has been cold, the ground frozen, and ice and snow cover the roads. The steep mountains are naturally sealed off, making troop movement particularly inconvenient. Once the weather warms up slightly, we will advance and severely suppress them. The bandits are surrounded on all sides and have nowhere to escape, but are merely prolonging their lives for a few days. As for within Shaanxi Province, the remnant bandits have been completely cleared, and the area is extremely peaceful. Because Sichuan and Shaanxi both have commanders, I accompanied Chairman Shao back to Wuhan and then to Jiangxi to meet Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, report on the progress of the pursuit and suppression, and request instructions on all matters. The question of whether to retain the Xi'an administrative office and whether I should return to Shaanxi will be decided after meeting with Chairman Chiang."

(Shao Lizhi's Statement) He stated briefly, "Because I have been separated from Chairman Chiang for a long time and am eager to meet him, I have specially requested a four-week leave from the Central Government to go to Jiangxi. The administrative affairs of Gansu Province have been temporarily entrusted to Director Deng Baoshan of the Gansu office of the Shaanxi Pacification Superintendent. My mission to Jiangxi, in addition to reporting to Chairman Chiang on the political situation in Gansu Province, is also to request to resign from my position as Provincial Chairman. After a short stay in Jiangxi, I will go to Nanjing to report to the Executive Yuan. As for the situation in Gansu Province, because it is located in the western frontier, there have been too many troops and too little production in the past. Coupled with natural and man-made disasters, the people are extremely impoverished, and the financial situation is very strained. Before I took office, government expenses were more than ten months in arrears, education expenses were more than twenty months in arrears, and debts owed to shops in Lanzhou amounted to more than 4.6 million, totaling over 8 to 9 million yuan including other debts. Despite my repeated efforts to reorganize, I am still short of 500,000 yuan. Moreover, the salaries of civil servants are no more than 80 yuan at the highest and 30 yuan at the lowest, making it difficult to maintain a living. The original Northwest and Peasant Banks in Lanzhou have now both gone bankrupt, financial activity is extremely sluggish, and commerce is also very depressed, so provincial administration has reached a dead end. With Gansu Province being barren and the people poor, such long-term deficits will be unsustainable in the future. Fortunately, the area is stable, and harmony between Han and Hui people alleviates the Central Government's concerns about the west. Ma Hongkui's troops have now returned to Ningxia, and Ma himself has arrived in Dingkou. He met with Director Yang in Shaanxi and they had a very pleasant conversation. Yang is busy and cannot go to Jiangxi for the time being. As for the recent invasion of Yuguan by Japanese soldiers, all Chinese people are indignant. The division and brigade commanders of Gansu Province have repeatedly telegraphed the Central Government requesting permission to send troops to resist the invaders. Public organizations and schools are particularly agitated." (February 2nd)

Strange Bird Discovered in Taihu Lake 91

In Wutangmen, Southern Spring, the 14th District, more than ten li from Taihu Lake, on Mount Tu, there is a villager named Ye, who makes a living by boat. The other day, he loaded goods from another village, unloaded them, and was sailing home. When he sailed near Mount Tu, he suddenly saw a black object floating on the lake, sometimes sinking and sometimes floating, resembling a corpse. Ye was curious, so he ordered his crew to pull it up. Unexpectedly, it was a huge strange bird that had frozen to death. Its entire body of feathers had turned grayish-white, and it weighed more than thirty catties. Its head was as big as a bamboo sieve, its eyes were like copper bells, and its toes had membranes, similar to a northern ostrich. At that time, Ye brought it back to Mount Tu, and the whole city was shocked. Crowds gathered to watch. Now, it is planned to take the bird to Shanghai for research.

City News

Northeast Association Holds Inaugural Meeting Yesterday 100

Elects Shi Liangcai and 26 Others as Directors

Plans to Recover Lost Territory and Develop Resources in the Future

Wu Tiecheng, Zhang Gongquan, Lin Kanghou, and others, recognizing the seriousness and importance of the Northeast problem, initiated the organization of the Northeast Association, which has been in preparation for several months. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the inaugural meeting was held on the ninth floor of the YMCA in Buxianqiao. Wu Tiecheng chaired the meeting, which passed the charter and elected 27 directors. Details are recorded below.

(Names of Attendees) Those who attended yesterday included Cai Yuanpei, Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, Chu Fucheng, Zhang Shizhao, Wu Tiecheng, Lin Kanghou, Shi Liangcai, Wang Yansong, Zheng Hongnian, Yu Qiaqing, Chen Binhe, Zang Qifang, Qi Shiying, Mu Ouchu, Huang Renzhi, Du Chongyuan, Lin Wojang, Wu Huanzhang, Jiang Songnian, Liu Piguang, Pang Yuedong, representatives of various Northeast armies, and more than 100 leaders from all walks of life and newspaper reporters.

(Chairman's Report) Chairman Wu Tiecheng reported on the origins of the association, stating briefly that the three northeastern provinces have 360,000 square miles of land, 30 million people, and countless treasures. Japan considers it a lifeline, and China considers it life itself. Without the Northeast, China has no way out. The three northeastern provinces have been lost for over a year. Our government has exhausted peaceful methods and the armed struggle of the Volunteer Army, but there is still no hope of recovery. Compatriots from the Northeast are coming to various parts of China to cry for help endlessly. Compatriots in the country are also actively providing assistance. There are organizations such as the Shanghai Relief for Northeast Refugees and the Liaoning-Jilin-Heilongjiang Volunteer Army Support Group. However, they are limited to relief and assistance. There is no unified organization. To save the Northeast, we must not only limit ourselves to relief. In addition, there are more important responsibilities. Therefore, we and others initiated the Northeast Association as a unified and permanent organization to save the Northeast. In addition to currently striving to recover the Northeast, we are also laying the foundation for developing the Northeast's resources in the future. This scope is greater than other organizations that only focus on relief, and the responsibility is also heavier.

(Summary of Speeches) Next, Cai Yuanpei spoke, stating briefly that all sectors in Shanghai have risen up to lead the country in assisting the Northeast, and there is great hope for the future of the Northeast. Because local associations have the experience of fully assisting the 19th Route Army in the January 28th Anti-Japanese War, it is a model for cooperation between the people and the army. We scholars do not seem to be of much help in the war, but in the Battle of Shanghai, scientists had an organization for technical cooperation, which achieved considerable results. In the future, we are still willing to do our best in this regard. Next, Chen Binhe spoke, stating briefly that Mayor Wu is very familiar with the situation in the Northeast and has said two things: "You don't know how vast China is until you go to the Northeast; you don't know how dangerous China is until you go to the Northeast." Chinese people study the Northeast after the September 18th Incident, while Japanese people study the Northeast before the Sino-Japanese War, a difference of decades. According to the Northeast Yearbook, last year the Japanese published 281 regular publications studying Manchuria and Mongolia, and 65 irregular publications, while China had only 38. Therefore, the Chinese people are far less familiar with the situation in the Northeast than the Japanese. The abundance of resources in the Northeast can be seen from the statistics of 1930 alone. Grain production reached 190 million tons, accounting for 20% of the national production. The Northeast is both a source of wealth and a source of disaster. Because the owners are not good at managing it, it has attracted the covetousness of thieves. The outbreak of disaster was before the September 18th Incident. There had already been two wars, the Sino-Japanese War and the Russo-Japanese War. It only became more serious after the September 18th Incident. Recently, Japanese Foreign Minister Uchida said in a speech in the parliament that even if Japan is turned into scorched earth, it will never leave Manchuria. This shows determination. The Japanese are willing to take the Northeast with iron and blood. We are determined to take it back with blood and iron. In world history, there is only the precedent of passively accepting oppression and national subjugation, but never resisting national subjugation. Finally, Ma Zhanshan's representative, Wu Huanzhang, spoke on behalf of the generals of the various Northeast Volunteer Armies, expressing gratitude and hope, and the necessity of fully assisting the Volunteer Armies so that they can maintain the source of power in Jilin and Heilongjiang.

(Charter Passed) Qi Shiying (from Liaoning), from the Secretariat of the Central Political Committee, read and amended the Northeast Association's charter item by item. Article 1: The name of this association is the Northeast Association. Article 2: The purpose of this association is to study the Northeast problem and to relieve Northeast compatriots. Article 3: This association is located in Shanghai and may establish branches in various provinces and cities. Article 4: Anyone who agrees with the purpose of this association, introduced by three or more members, and approved by the Board of Directors, may become a member of this association. Article 5: The General Assembly of Members is the highest decision-making body of this association and shall meet once every six months. Extraordinary meetings may be convened by the Board of Directors when necessary. Article 6: This association shall elect thirty-five persons as Directors from the General Assembly of Members to form the Board of Directors. Their term of office is one year and they may be re-elected. Article 7: The Board of Directors shall meet once a month, and extraordinary meetings may be convened when necessary. Article 8: The responsibilities of the Board of Directors are as follows: (1) To implement the resolutions of the General Assembly of Members; (2) To plan and manage financial matters; (3) To decide on the work plan of this association and to implement it; (4) To supervise the activities of local branches and to contact other organizations assisting the Northeast; (5) To discuss other matters. Article 9: The Board of Directors shall appoint one Secretary-General, who shall be publicly elected by the Directors and shall carry out the affairs of the association under the direction of the Board of Directors. Article 10: The Board of Directors shall establish five groups: General Affairs, Organization, Investigation, Relief, and Propaganda. Special committees may be established by the Board of Directors when necessary. (1) The General Affairs Group shall handle all routine affairs of the association, including documents, general affairs, accounting, and other daily affairs. (2) The Organization Group shall handle matters relating to member registration and the organization of local branches. (3) The Investigation Group shall handle matters relating to the investigation, research, and compilation of all matters relating to the Northeast problem. (4) The Relief Group shall handle matters relating to assisting and relieving Northeast people and guiding them. (5) The Propaganda Group shall handle matters relating to promoting the culture and national thought of our Northeast. Article 11: Each group shall have one Director-General and a number of staff members, who shall be under the direction of the Secretary-General and shall manage the affairs of their respective groups. The Director-General and staff members shall be nominated by the Secretary-General and appointed by the Board of Directors. Article 12: The funds of this association shall be financed by the following items of income: (1) Membership fees; (2) Special donations; (3) Subsidies.

Article 13: If a member of this association violates the charter or the resolutions of the General Assembly and the Board of Directors, the Board of Directors may resolve to revoke their membership and submit it to the General Assembly of Members for ratification. Article 14: The rules of procedure for meetings of the Board of Directors and the rules of procedure for the various groups shall be determined separately. Article 15: This charter shall be implemented from the date of passage by the General Assembly of Members. If there are any imperfections, they may be submitted to the General Assembly of Members for amendment upon the proposal of one-fifth or more of the members or upon the resolution of the Board of Directors.

(Election of Directors) According to the charter, the directors of the association should be thirty-five people, but because there are not many members now, Lin Kanghou proposed to first elect twenty-seven people. The chairman nominated them, sought the consent of all, and voted to pass them. Chairman Wu Tiecheng then nominated and introduced the twenty-seven people one by one and they passed. The remaining eight people will be added after the membership increases. The names of the twenty-seven people elected are as follows: Shi Liangcai, Wang Xiaolai, Yu Qiaqing, Zhu Qinglan, Xiong Xiling, Wang Zhengting, Wang Zhuoran (President of the Northeast Diplomatic Association), Wang Xianzhang (a prominent figure in Heilongjiang), Mi Chunlin, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Gongquan, Wang Shuhan, Lin Kanghou, Du Chongdao, Chu Fucheng, Yang Hu, Wu Xingya, Qi Shiying, Zang Qifang, Chen Lifu, Li Xi'en (President of Jilin University), Cheng Yun, Ye Xiufeng, Wang Yansong, Xiao Zhenying, Wu Tiecheng, Li Denghui.

(Determination of Address) The first meeting of the association will be convened in the short term. The association's office is temporarily located in the China Aviation Association at 99 Jessfield Road. Yesterday, the YMCA venue displayed various Japanese books on the Northeast and Japanese Manchurian textbooks for people to browse. Liu Piguang, the representative of Li Du, also brought paper money issued by the Central Bank of the Puppet State. Its form is the same as that of the Bank of Korea, which proves that the Puppet State is completely colonized.

Local Association Receives Telegram from Kailu 103

丨Four Enemy Planes Shot Down丨

(Telegram from Kailu) The local association received a telegram from Cui Xinwu of Kailu stating the entire story of the enemy's attack on Kailu in detail: Recently, the enemy saw a sudden increase in the number of volunteer troops and Jiang province retreating soldiers in Kailu, fearing they would advance on Tongliao. They used the tactic of defeating the enemy one by one, first using a large number of aircraft to bomb the county seat for days on end, causing excessive damage to our forces, which had no choice but to find a way to relocate. This left only a portion of the brigade commander's forces to defend independently. Then, they used a large force to attack the front lines. After succeeding, they were able to obtain Kailu without a fight. Then, on the morning of a certain day, seventy Japanese soldiers suddenly arrived, along with over a thousand Mongolian soldiers and Zhang HaiPeng's troops, accompanied by four armored vehicles. Later, tanks, planes, mountain guns, and machine guns launched a fierce attack on our Daodeyingzi defense line. In one day, they fiercely attacked our position three times, using machine guns and mountain guns from below, and a large number of bombers from above, bombing as much as possible. The number of our troops on the front line was less than a regiment of cavalry. The enemy's artillery and bombs completely destroyed the position and the Daodeyingzi regimental headquarters beyond recognition. However, our soldiers used cover and did not decrease in number, still calmly killing the enemy with rifles, mortars, hand grenades, and broadswords. Then, as the enemy planes flew low, they used rifles to shoot upwards at the planes. The battle lasted until about 6 p.m., when the enemy ran out of strength and retreated across the entire line. After a detailed investigation after the battle, more than ten Japanese soldiers and more than forty puppet troops were killed, and four enemy planes were shot down. One was burned by us, and the other three fell within the enemy's battle line, so they were transported back to Tongliao by vehicle. Thanks to our divine protection, only more than ten cavalry horses and five soldiers were injured, and the rest were all unharmed. Now, because the wireless telegraph was destroyed by the enemy's bombing, and the wired telegraph was also bombed in several sections, the telegram was delayed. Respectfully submitted, Brigade Commander Cui Xinwu kowtows with reverence," etc. Respectfully submitted, Winter Seal.

Dismissing Resignation, Details Recorded Separately Below

(Resignation Process) Since taking office, although Minister Chen had plans to develop the navy, it was difficult to make bricks without straw. Ultimately, due to financial difficulties, not only could the development plans not be realized, but even the current situation was difficult to maintain. During the January 28th Incident, the navy did not participate in the fighting because it did not receive orders from the government, which led to criticism from the people. All of this was the reason for Minister Chen's pessimism. Towards the end of last month, Minister Chen resolutely submitted his resignation to the Executive Yuan, and at the same time issued a notice to all his subordinates, stating the pain of his resignation and instructing them to serve with peace of mind. Minister Chen himself quietly came to Shanghai on the 30th of last month and resided at the Hui Zhong Hotel on the Bund. After President Song received Minister Chen's resignation, in addition to instructing him to stay, he also telegraphed Secretary-General Chu Minyi of the Executive Yuan, who came to Shanghai yesterday to convey the government's intention to persuade him to stay.

(Chu Minyi's Remarks) Secretary-General Chu arrived in Shanghai at about 8:00 a.m. yesterday and immediately returned to his residence to rest. He then drove to visit Minister Chen at the Hui Zhong Hotel and talked for about an hour before leaving. According to Secretary-General Chu, speaking to a reporter from the Central News Agency, there are three reasons for Minister Chen's resignation: (1) poor health, (2) financial difficulties in the navy, and (3) misunderstanding and repeated criticism from the outside world, so he resigned pessimistically. I was ordered by President Song to come to Shanghai to persuade him to stay and discuss the difficulties. The result was extremely satisfactory. Minister Chen has agreed to dismiss his resignation and will go to Nanjing to resume his post in a few days.

(Chen Shaokuan's Remarks) The reporter also visited Minister Chen at the Hui Zhong Hotel to ask if he had dismissed his intention to resign. According to Chen, since I have served as the head of the navy, I have not achieved any results. Thinking of this, I feel ashamed to the people of the country. I submitted my resignation last year, but it has not been approved. Considering the current time of internal and external troubles, the navy is of utmost importance to national defense, so I have decided to resign to make way for the capable, so that the navy can be expanded as soon as possible, and national defense can be consolidated. And my determination to leave is firm. After resigning, I intend to participate in the anti-Japanese war as a citizen. Recalling the Shanghai war last year, the navy did not assist the 19th Route Army in the anti-Japanese war because it did not receive orders, which I have always regarded as a lifelong pain. Because the deployment of warships must obey the orders of superiors, but the people do not understand and criticize each other, which is truly regrettable. Chen also said that the navy's finances are extremely tight. Although the prescribed monthly funding is 500,000 yuan, in reality only 400,000 yuan is received, while the expenses of various departments under the ministry are enormous, and money is needed everywhere. Compared with the naval budgets of European and American countries, there is a world of difference. It is imperative to find ways to expand.

He should be able to return to Nanjing after about a week of recuperation.

Shanghai's Methods for Reducing and Exempting Land Rent 106

Divided into Four Grades, Approved by the Municipal Government

The Municipal Government previously issued an order regarding the reduction and exemption of land rent in Shanghai, instructing the Social Affairs Bureau to draft a method. Upon receiving the order, the bureau inquired about the methods approved and implemented in neighboring counties in Shanghai and instructed the municipal commissioners and farmers' associations in various war zones in Shanghai to investigate and report. After referring to the situation of land tax reduction and exemption in various districts, the bureau drafted a rent reduction method a few days ago and submitted it to the municipal government for review and implementation. The municipal government, upon receiving the report, proposed it to the municipal council for discussion and decided to pass it according to the original proposed method. Yesterday, the bureau was instructed to publish it in accordance with the resolution. The rent reduction method is divided into four grades: (1) Districts that have been approved for land tax reduction and exemption of 20% or less will have their original land rent reduced by 30%; (2) Those with land tax exemptions of 30% to 40% will have their original land rent reduced by 40%; (3) Those with land tax exemptions of 50% to 60% will have their original land rent reduced by 50%; (4) Those with land tax exemptions of 70% or more will have their original land rent reduced by 60%.

Regarding the abolition of various donation names and single tax items, the Finance Office should investigate the nature of the double levy of dou donations in the six counties outside the Pass, the additional levy of livestock brokerage tax and livestock fees in each county, as well as the scale brokerage tax in Yanqing County and the native cloth brokerage tax in Huai'an and Wanquan counties, and correct them separately. Regarding the collection of business tax at the rate of business tax in Hebei Province, the Zhejiang Provincial Provisional Measures for the Continued Collection of Business Tax are amended to use three levels of tax rates: 0.5%, 0.8%, and 1%. The Chahar Provincial Business Tax Collection Regulations can also be re-drafted with reference to this. This Ministry has issued another order to the Finance Office to re-draft the regulations and send them to the Ministry for review and approval. Whether the rate of business tax in Chahar Province should be re-drafted with reference to the Hebei Provincial Collection Regulations shall be considered and drafted by the Finance Office in light of local conditions in order to be appropriate. As for the assistance of Chahar Province to Hebei's military expenditure, it is a matter of consultation between the two provinces and should be handled directly by Chahar Province in consultation with Hebei Province. In addition to instructing the Chahar Provincial Finance Office to comply with the instructions for reference and handle separately, the approval is hereby issued for reference. Ministry of Finance, Seal." After receiving the telegram, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce has notified the Chahar Provincial representatives for reference.

Municipal Government Organizes Committee for the Use of National Products 111

The municipal government previously received the Executive Yuan's promulgated method for public officials to use national products. The city should also establish a committee for the use of national products. Therefore, the case was submitted to the municipal council for discussion a few days ago and it was decided to appoint the first section chiefs of each bureau as members, and designate a member of the secretariat as the chairman. It is reported that yesterday, in accordance with the resolution, the first section chiefs of each bureau were ordered to organize the committee. The provisions of the method promulgated by the Executive Yuan regarding the powers of the committee are recorded below: (A) Investigate the products and types of domestic products for use by various agencies; (B) Formulate the deadline for all personnel of each agency to wear uniforms, and the uniforms must be made of domestic products; (C) Advise public officials of each agency not to purchase non-domestic clothing in the future, and existing non-domestic clothing may be worn temporarily within the deadline; (D) Supervise each agency to give priority to the use of domestic products when purchasing official supplies. The detailed methods for the foregoing clauses and the deadline for wearing uniforms shall be determined by each committee.

Bank Clearing House Implements Continued Handling of Silver Dollar Remittances 112

Handling of Sycee Transfers to Resume on the 16th

Four Types to Be Fully Completed by March 1

Expanded Site and Established Holiday Method

The Joint Preparatory Committee of the Bankers' Association, which also operates the clearing house, has been handling silver dollar transfers since it opened on January 10. Starting on February 1, silver dollar remittances will be handled, and the 5th Committee meeting established a holiday method. Details are as follows:

(Expanded Site) There are 22 clearing banks in the clearing house, including the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, and the Four Banks Savings Association. The office is located in the west end of the Bank Association building at 4 Hong Kong Road, the former site of the Public Debt Fund Custody Committee. Because the space is insufficient, it was moved to the Great Auditorium at the end of last month. The center is the manager's platform, the east end is the report platform, and the west is the clearing platform. There are 32 platforms surrounded by iron mesh on both sides, one for each clearing bank. When silver dollar transfers were first handled, each bank sent at least two clearing clerks. Since February 1, when silver dollar remittances were handled, each bank has sent at least three clearing clerks.

(Gradual Progress) A reporter from the New Sound News Agency met with Zhu Puquan, the manager of the clearing house, last night. According to him, according to Article 20 of the regulations, clearing banks should open the following four types of currency current accounts in the association to pay and receive clearing differences: (1) silver dollar transfers, (2) sycee transfers, (3) silver dollar remittances, (4) sycee remittances. When the clearing house opened, it first handled silver dollar transfers. Starting on February 1, it continued to handle silver dollar remittances. It was decided that sycee transfers would be resumed on February 16, and sycee remittances would be resumed on March 1. At that time, the four types will be fully completed.

(Holiday Method) The Clearing House Committee held its fifth meeting on January 24 and decided to establish the following holiday method for clearing: (1) The association's holidays shall be in accordance with the regulations of the Bankers' Association. Clearing shall be suspended on the association's holidays; (2) Clearing banks that take holidays other than the association's holidays shall not participate in clearing during the holiday period, but shall notify the association in advance, and the association shall notify all banks. Bills of exchange from banks that are on holiday cannot be submitted for clearing during the holiday period; (3) On the full-day holidays of Bund banks other than the association's holidays, the types of currency for clearing shall be limited to remittances. On the half-day afternoon holidays of Bund banks other than the association's holidays, the clearing time and currency types on that day shall be in accordance with the regulations on Saturdays; (4) When the types of currency for clearing are limited to remittances, transfers between participating clearing banks may be deemed to be submitted for clearing as remittances; (5) During the holidays in Article 3, the receipts and disbursements of the remittance current accounts of the various clearing banks of the association shall be handled as usual by the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. Zhu Puquan, the manager, has already notified everyone to comply with the regulations yesterday.

Overview of Municipal Finance for Half a Year 113

Expenditure of More Than 5.3 Million Yuan

Deficit of More Than 1.14 Million Yuan

Since the January 28th Incident, the vitality of Shanghai has not been fully restored. The revenue and expenditure of the Municipal Finance Bureau this year is still abnormally exhausted. It is reported that the income from various donations and taxes from July to December was about 4.2 million yuan, a decrease of about 700,000 yuan compared to the original budget income. However, except for the business tax, which has not been implemented due to the special circumstances of Shanghai, and the land tax, which has a relatively short collection, the remaining taxes, such as house donations, have no shortages compared to the budget. Even compared to the calculated amount in the 20th year of the Republic, there are surpluses and no deficits. The expenditure of various expenses is mainly due to the sharp increase in post-war expenses, totaling about 5.3 million yuan. Among them, the recurring expenses include party affairs expenses of more than 72,000 yuan, administrative expenses of more than 131,000 yuan, public security expenses of more than 884,000 yuan, financial expenses of more than 141,000 yuan, education and cultural expenses of more than 432,000 yuan, social expenses of more than 90,000 yuan, public utility expenses of more than 98,000 yuan, health expenses of more than 119,000 yuan, engineering construction expenses of more than 436,000 yuan, land expenses of more than 49,000 yuan, municipal expenses of more than 23,000 yuan, assistance expenses of more than 108,000 yuan, debt expenses of more than 324,000 yuan, other expenses of more than 58,000 yuan, and the recurring expenses of the Security Office in November and December of more than 140,000 yuan, totaling more than 3.111 million yuan. The temporary expenses include party affairs expenses of 3,000 yuan, administrative expenses of more than 535,000 yuan (the expenses of the Security Office before November were paid by the municipal government here), public security expenses of more than 462,000 yuan, financial expenses of more than 44,000 yuan, education and cultural expenses of more than 299,000 yuan, social expenses of more than 54,000 yuan, public utility expenses of more than 97,000 yuan, health expenses of more than 18,000 yuan, engineering construction expenses of more than 622,000 yuan, land expenses of more than 72,000 yuan, more than 3,000 yuan for each city area, assistance expenses of more than 8,000 yuan, and other expenses of more than 3,000 yuan, totaling more than 2.234 million yuan. The revenue and expenditure are offset by a deficit of more than 1.144 million yuan, which has been dealt with by the municipal financial authorities by raising funds.

China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Beijing Line Temporarily Reduces Flights 114

Two Round Trips Per Week

Can Be Restored After One Month

Since the opening of the China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Beijing line, it has been quite developed, with three round trips per week, and both mail and passengers have increased. It is now learned that the company has suddenly reduced flights since this month, setting it to fly north from Shanghai to Beijing every Tuesday and Saturday, and fly south from Beijing to Shanghai every Wednesday, which actually reduces one round trip per week. According to Li Diezhuang, the secretary of the company, there are two reasons for the reduction: (1) too few aircraft, (2) too few pilots. Because the aircraft body needs to be repaired frequently, it can be used for a long time, otherwise it is inevitable that there will be danger. The pilots also feel too tired from driving every day. If they fly every day, the aircraft body and the pilots will have no chance to rest. It is impossible to reduce it to twice a week, but it is also temporary. Once the board of directors is held in the middle of this month, aircraft will be added and pilots will be hired to restore the original state and increase business.

Severe Cold Weather Causes Inner River Boats in Jiangsu to be Icebound Again 115

The weather this year is exceptionally cold, more so than in previous years. On January 10th, small boats on the inner rivers of Jiangsu province were icebound. Those boats in the Gaodian area were stuck for over ten days. Just as navigation resumed, it coincided with the end of the old lunar year. The first voyage after the lunar new year was met with another cold front, causing the inner rivers of Jiangsu to be icebound again for the second time. According to a source from the inland river boat bureau whom this reporter consulted yesterday, the prolonged drought last year caused the water levels in the various river ports to be very shallow. By mid-November of last year, some small boats in various locations could not operate due to the low water levels. When the severe cold arrived last month, shallow river ports were more easily frozen. During the first ice blockage, the ice chunks in the river had not completely melted when the boats resumed operation. Therefore, this time, with the invasion of cold winds, it was even easier for ice to form. The frozen routes include the Xili Line, Changyang Line, Sudang Line, Zhenqing Line, Changli Line, as well as other inland routes, all of which are affected by ice. However, it is not a complete blockage of the entire line, but rather only the shallowest sections of the river, accounting for about one-third of the entire route. From February 1st onwards, many routes were blocked and impassable. Some boats were even stranded mid-journey due to the ice. There are even more civilian boats being blocked by the ice than small boats. As of today, they have not yet resumed operation. Upon receiving the news, the various shipping companies immediately dispatched civilian boats carrying ice-breaking equipment and hired workers to the frozen areas, planning to break the ice section by section to open up the waterways. However, the ice in the shallow areas is over a foot thick, which is beyond human power to break. This plan has completely failed. Passengers who were delayed due to the ice have been taking the risk of stepping onto the ice to reach the shore and walking to various towns and cities. Their luggage and belongings are being transported by local villagers for a fee, who also serve as guides. The boats trapped by the ice have reported to the water police, requesting protection while waiting for the ice to melt before resuming operation. According to Mr. Zhang Jianfei, the owner of the Inland Merchants Bureau, after the second ice blockage of inland boats and civilian boats, the Shanghai-Suzhou, Shanghai-Hangzhou, and Shanghai-Lake lines, although not directly blocked by ice, have also been indirectly affected by the traffic disruption in terms of business. This is because the majority of inland passengers and goods are stuck midway and cannot be transferred to Shanghai. Therefore, the number of passengers and goods traveling on the Shanghai-Suzhou boats recently has been exceptionally low.

Mediation by Director Du Resolves the Merchants Bureau's Layoff of Dock Workers 116

Each person receives an additional month's severance pay.

Payment available today, but only for union members.

After the Merchants Bureau announced the layoff of 101 dock workers due to financial difficulties, each worker was to be paid two months' salary as severance pay, one month's salary for January, and a double salary for December. As a result, directors Yang and Du personally provided an additional month's severance pay to each laid-off worker, but only to union members. The union immediately reported this to the laid-off members, who all accepted the mediation by directors Du and Yang. Decide to Form an Unemployed Appeal Group

Over seventy Southern Goods stores, including Shao Wansheng, Tongtaiding, Yuelaixin, Dechangshun, Tongfengxiang, Ruifengmao, etc., dismissed over 120 workers, including Fei Zugen, Yu Daokun, and Wang Shiliang, during the Lunar New Year. However, they were suddenly dismissed on January 29th, and they requested negotiation for reinstatement. The union sent a member to negotiate, but was repeatedly rejected, and the issue has not been resolved. On February 1st, the dismissal of personnel was announced, and all were immediately required to leave the stores without food or lodging. Plans to Promote the Sale of Stored Silk 130

The Ministry of Industry previously noted that the sale of silk by foreign firms had plummeted, and the number of stored silk and cocoons in silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang was very large, making it impossible to sell them, threatening bankruptcy. Therefore, it specially sent personnel to jointly organize two committees with leaders of silk factories: the Committee for the Arrangement of Stored Factory Silk and Stored Dry Cocoons and the Committee for Sales, to conduct the work separately. It is learned that since its establishment last winter, the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Committee for the Sale of Stored Factory Silk, under the active promotion of Director He Bingxian, has sold 40-50% of the stored factory silk. However, the remaining silk is still substantial, and efforts should be made to make progress. Since Chinese silk merchants have traditionally relied on foreign firms to sell futures silk, resulting in many barriers, and since the European and American raw silk markets fluctuate from time to time, and the exchange rate rises and falls daily, it is urgently necessary to engage in direct trade. Therefore, the association decided to continue to handle the spot sales of raw silk, purchasing it at actual prices and dividing it into two departments: remittance and consignment sales, and directly transporting it to the American market for sale. The required funds have now been presented to the Ministry of Industry for allocation to Shanghai and were formally implemented the day before yesterday (i.e., the 1st). In recent days, manufacturers have been entrusting the association to promote the sale of spot factory silk in droves, and Director He has personally contacted them.

Page 16

Social Affairs Bureau Strictly Prohibits Fabricating Weights and Measures 133

丨Those who hawk them will be dealt with according to law丨

The Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau instructed the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, stating the following: The Municipal Weights and Measures Inspection Office reported that its duties are the inspection of weights and measures, and it does not handle the manufacturing or sale of such instruments. The collection of inspection fees is based on regulations stipulated by the ministry, and the amount is extremely small, which should have no impact on the manufacturing costs of merchants. However, recently, a few manufacturers of weights and measures, taking advantage of the fact that various industries are now voluntarily adopting the new system and the demand for new instruments is urgent, have taken the opportunity to raise prices and falsely claim that a high inspection fee must be paid when submitting for inspection. Some have even fabricated the names of official instruments to deceive and hawk them, seeking exorbitant profits. What is even more surprising is that the Shen Xin and other newspapers published on the 22nd of this month contained a notice from the Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry Association stating that the required weighing instruments had been purchased from the Inspection Office by members of the association. This misunderstanding may have arisen because the association did not clearly identify the place of purchase, which could lead to the spread of misinformation.

Now that unscrupulous individuals are using deceitful words to swindle, it will only confuse matters further, and the city's efforts to manage weights and measures, which should have a good reputation, will be seen as motivated by profit. This will not only hinder progress but also damage credibility. In addition to the fact that the office will continue to collect weights and measures inspection fees in accordance with the regulations stipulated by the ministry, and will not engage in manufacturing or sales, and will directly send a letter to the Bean and Rice Industry Association clarifying the misunderstanding, and will strictly order all weights and measures manufacturers not to take advantage of the widespread adoption of the new system to raise prices and hawk newly invented instruments, it is appropriate to submit a document to you, hoping that you will order the various industry associations to notify their members that if they encounter the aforementioned price increases and hawking of newly invented instruments, they should report them to the nearest public security agency for legal action to facilitate implementation and deter cunning fraud. This order is for your association to comply with, and to instruct all industry associations to inform their members accordingly.

Measures for Issuing Practicing Certificates for Western Doctors 134

For those not registered and licensed before 1929

Since the Ministry of Interior promulgated the Physician’s Provisional Certification Measures in July of last year, some Western doctors in the city who had not registered and obtained licenses from the Municipal Health Bureau before 1929 found that the Provisional Certification Measures were not applicable to them. They have requested the Municipal Health Bureau to issue practicing certificates so that they could apply for certification from the Ministry. The bureau then submitted a request to the Municipal Government, which ordered them to formulate measures for this purpose. It is now reported that the bureau has drafted these measures and submitted them to the Municipal Government, which approved them for implementation on January 23 of this year. The following is an excerpt: (Measures for Western Doctors in Shanghai Who Have Not Registered and Obtained Licenses Before 1929 to Apply for Practicing Certificates) (1) Any Western doctor who meets the qualifications specified in Article 2, Paragraph 1 of the Physician's Provisional Certification Measures promulgated by the Ministry of Interior (i.e., has completed more than five years of internship in a well-equipped hospital) and who has practiced in the city before 1929 may apply to the Health Bureau for a practicing certificate. (2) When applying for a practicing certificate, the following documents must be submitted: A. A certificate from the hospital where the applicant completed more than five years of internship; B. Documents proving that the applicant practiced before 1929: (1) An advertisement in a well-known newspaper before 1929; (2) A prescription issued before 1929, which has been filled by a pharmacy and stamped with the pharmacy's seal, after verification; (3) A listing of the clinic or hospital in a telephone directory before 1929, sufficient to prove that the applicant was practicing; (4) A joint affidavit from three or more doctors who held licenses issued by the bureau in 1927 or 1928. If one type of proof is insufficient, the applicant may be ordered to provide additional proofs. C. A resume; D. Two two-and-a-half-inch portrait photos. These measures will be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government and will expire after three months.

Large Number of Refugees Passing Through 135

Rations Distributed and Travel Expenses Provided

Four hundred and some male and female refugees from Xiangtan, Hunan, suddenly arrived at Hongqiao Town in western Shanghai the other day. Their representatives, Wang Shien and Liu Guiqiu, requested rice and firewood from local stores. The merchants in the town found it difficult to provide for so many people. Chen Dekui, the police chief of the town's police station, sent officers to maintain order. As there were no empty houses in the town, they were led to the Anguo Temple and Pengchang Temple, about three li from the town, for temporary shelter. Yesterday, personnel from the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau went to the countryside to distribute rations and provide some travel expenses to each person. Therefore, the local area was not disturbed. According to the representatives, the Xiangtan area has suffered from natural disasters and banditry for years, and the people have been displaced. Once the weather warms up, they plan to return to their hometowns to farm. They do not plan to stay here for long and intend to depart the day after tomorrow, heading west along the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway.
